Do you guys know that the Shuffle dance came from 1990's dance called 'New Jack Swing'? Basically, the Shuffle took all the footwork from New Jack-Swing. That's why 90's dance music goes so well with the Shuffle, it's not accidental. If you check out dance music videos from the 90's, you can see the footwork is the same.

Overall great but disappointed with the "Side" Step. Although it was incorrect how you demonstrated, it's called a T-Step and it is the fundamental root of why shuffling even exists in the first place. It requires a heel and toe movement of one foot while the other foot is raised and then planted behind the moving foot. After proper practice and raising the speed to be able to go on simple beats, you can then place the raising foot anywhere you like. The T-Step helps with making a smoother look to your shuffle, giving the illusion that you are gliding around.

wow
Oh, I was doing this in the 90's already, before I heard it called 'shuffling'. Well, my mother tongue isn't English, so maybe people did have that name then already. I just saw it on the dance floor, tried it, and it was goooood (Jim Carrie voice, if you want). I especially enjoed the feeling you get there, that you're 'light foot'. The same reason we like to swing as kids, to feel lighter.  The main philosophy is to kick yourself a bit above the floor, and make the turns ans shuffles when you feel 'you're light', meaning you have a light touch with the floor. Normally, just after you kicked yourself up from the 'bottom', from the floor. So plan to make the moves immediately after you've kicked the start to your move from the floor.   You're making the important moves with the ball of your foot, usually as soon as your heel (your main weight) has left the floor. Hanging a bit higher in the room :) For a few fractions of time. With frequent kicks, you'll be feeling you're mostly a bit off the floor, you're a bit lighter. And the kicks are there to express your joy, you feel kiddy giddy :) Or am I wrong, was it giddy kiddy?! :) Best advice, have fun with it, it really kicks butt... upwards.  For example, in the Running man shuffle, you kick yourself upwards, and while going, the kicking foot starts to 'slip' backwards (actually you slide it intentionally right away when you 'leave the floor'). Then you come down to correct the slip with the other foot, that kicks you up, and then 'slips', and you keep on 'running'.   You can add to the upwards kick a slight push backward, just to move a bit, if yu don't feel like dancing on the same spot anymore. You can even twist while you're going, doing 180 turn (half turn). See who's dancing in that part of the dance floor. Maybe someone who's been staring at your butt :) I'm a guy, so if you're girl, you know our eyes don't always focus on your hair or eyes... Of course guys might be staring at guys and girls at girls, and it's their business. I just don't see a very fruitful future with that.  Once you've made some successful moves, and feel you've got the hang of it, with some moves, just try to move to different directions, sideways, forward, backward, on your spot (like the running man). Just test what feels fun, and how your joints and mass can move to different directions. Hve fun like a kid, don't be too serious or slavishly follow 'the dance teacher's advice'. That's a start, but the whole style is based on improvising, how you feel the beat. Kick yourself to the motion with the beat, and feel with the ball of your foot, which way I could shuffle, or twist.  The flexible shoes are needed because of the friction the shuffles and twists make, especially when sometimes you turn when the weight is full on the shoe, no matter how skillful you are :)
